My last moving experience with another company was not so great, so I was skeptical when choosing a new mover. This experience with H2H was extremely pleasant. From the start they gave me an hourly rate discount for a cash payment, which on my limited budget help immensely.

The communication was superb with H2H, they called me the evening before to confirm I was still on track, I received a text message in the morning with an ETA, and the guys called me a few minutes before their arrival.

The two gentlemen that came out to do the move were very professional, polite, and clean. They listened and accommodated all my needs and addressed my concerns. Being hourly, I made the incorrect assumption they would drag their feet a little to bring up the hours work, boy was I wrong, they moved swiftly and kept assuring me that the move would be quick.

<time>1627584192064</time>< rating>
1< /rating>
< review>
On May 13, 2021 we brought our 2008 Jaguar Vanden Plas to European-AutoWerks for the reason of correcting the CATS system fault. They had the car for three weeks, returning it to us with more problems than it had when we left it with them.

They replaced a connector to one of the struts, causing the CATS system fault code to go away. Their inspection of the rest of the car revealed a ‚Äúseverely‚Äù leaking rack and pinion. This was approved by us for replacing. These two repairs cost us over $2200.

As mentioned above, they had the car for three weeks. Every day I would call and ask for an update, to which they would replay, ‚Äútomorrow or the next day, at the latest.‚Äù I would call again the next day , requesting an update, to which they would replay, ‚Äútomorrow or the next day, at the latest.‚Äù This went on for three weeks.

On June 2, 2021, while on our way to European-AutoWerks to pick up our car, we were called by them and  informed that the air conditioning motor had failed and needed to be replaced. Their recommendation regarding the replacement of the motor was based on, as they stated, the motor getting electrical current and not turning. We declined. Upon entering the car we found that the driver side seat would not move. They checked for codes and none were found. I suggested that it was a fuse. This notion was countered by them stating that it would have showed up on the code reader. Later that afternoon, I examined the fuses, find one that was burnt. After replacing that fuse both the air conditioning motor and the seat started working. It seems very strange that the motor would receive electrical current with a burnt fuse in the circuit.

During our drive home, the CATS system fault warning, the original problem, came on again. The next day the power steering began to malfunction. This time we decided to take the car to Hoehn Jaguar Land Rover in Carlsbad, not being able to be without our car for another three weeks. They found that while replacing the connector on the strut European-AutoWerks incorrectly routed the wires over the exhaust, causing the wires to burn. They also found that while replacing the rack and pinion they incorrectly routed those wires, causing them to burn as well. Hoehn was able to correct both in two days.

When I contacted them regarding these issues, seeking restitution, they politely replied that they had nothing to do with these problems, except the power steering failure, which they ignored completely. When I emailed them back regarding the power steering, they refused to respond.

<Pics>None< /Pics><Text>I requested an appointment through their website during the weekend to get my 07 Mini Cooper S into the shop first thing Monday morning. I received a response promptly Monday morning prior to their store hours that accommodated my request. Jason was helpful and respectful from the get-go. I identified that I had an oil leak and was losing a substantial amount of fluid in a short amount of time and my idle fluctuating between 600-800RPM; not constant. The job required the front end of the car to be disassembled to locate and isolate the leak(s). They identified that the oil cooler gasket and oil filter stand gasket were the cause of my problems. They called me to inform me of the problem and solution prior to conducting the work. Through the process, e-mailed pictures of the location of the leak and the disassembly. They checked all my fluids while conducting the repairs, and informed me that the car was well over due for transmission fluid (provided photos as well). I recently bought the car used with 68k miles, and wouldn't be surprised if it was the original fluid, so I had them change it as well. I also needed new air mass meter boot, the original was held on by the hose clamp tied to a metal hose by a wire. With the amount of work to be done, my car had to be left over night to finish up the work the next day (Tuesday). Jason called me mid morning to tell me everything was put back together and that the engine makes a terrible 'hiss'. Being the boot had been faulty, and likely leaking--not creating a sufficient seal the hiss wasn't noticeable. The PVC valve's diaphragm was faulty and on the verge of failing which would have created a vacuum within the engine and displaced the engine oil. I authorized to have the valve cover replaced (PVC is embedded within). I picked up my Cooper Tuesday evening. She sounded great. I no longer had an idle problem. She ran great. I am a happy customer. I HIGHLY recommend them. I will be a return customer!! Thanks again guys!</Text></record>

Worst customer service ever!!!
I had shutters installed in 3 bedrooms back in July. They are inside mounts and supposed to be directly on top of the window molding. i believe they were measured wrong because they don't look right (molding is sticking out here and there on 3 of them). i called their customer service and told them about this and they emailed me a link to their support website. I filled out a complaint and uploaded pictures of the shutters to their website. I received this email from them the day after  -
Mychael Margott (Window Design Group)
Jul 23, 1:23 PM PDT

Mr. Hamilton,

you will be hearing from our scheduling team today. We will be taking new measurements and we will be remaking the shutters that are not covering your molding properly. I am very sorry that this has happened. We will take 110% care of you moving forward on this.

Thank you so much,

Mychael
Window Design Group Support Staff

Their guy came over on July 28 and took measurements for replacement shutters. about 7 weeks later ( the installed shutters took 6 weeks to be made, so I thought I would be hearing from them) I sent emails asking for an update on my replacement shutters. No response. They have a number you can text so I texted them on Friday, Sept 7 asking for an update. Here's their response:
Hello James,
After reviewing the inspection report that Eli sent in, he stated that the install was complete & everything was fine. There is nothing stating for anything to be reordered. Can you please provide pictures of the product that you think needs to be repaired?

I  told them that I had an email from them saying shutters would be remade and everything would be taken care of. Their response was that they would review this matter with Myke and get back to me on Monday.
I text them on Tuesday saying it's Tuesday and I still have no idea when I'm getting replacement shutters. No response. I call them on Wednesday and Tanya says that the install was fine and if I could upload pictures of the shutters I thought were off. I uploaded pictures on their support website again that night and their response the next day was this:

Tanya Bramson (Window Design Group)
Sep 13, 4:55 PM PDT

Hi Mr. Hamilton,

I have reviewed this with Mychael as well as Eli (the measure tech). The shutters are absolutely as they should be. I understand that you are frustrated and we never want that for any customer.
Window Design Group Support Staff

Here's the thing, the shutters are NOT as they should be! Do yourselves a favor and steer clear from this company, do a lot of research before using anyone. Google "Ca contractors license search" and use the Better Business Bureau and Yelp to look at complaints against a company. If I had done this with Window Design Group, I would have used someone else for sure. And if they think I am from a competitor trying to slander them, I'm not. I am ticket number 1434 on your support website. Communication with this company is a joke.</Review>

< Review>
I took a handful of bids for my project which included shutters for 7 windows and rolling shades for two sliders. While shutter products did not seems to vary greatly from company to company, pricing of bids and quality of salesmanship varied quite a bit. In the end, I was most impressed by WDG's salesperson Stephen S. and the quality of both the company's product and very competitive price.

I was a little concerned before installation because of some delay caused by the holidays and some sort of machine failure (see other reviews for similar tales of woe), but in the end the product was delivered and installed in a timely fashion.

Installation was a breeze -- right on time, professionally done, in and out. The shutters look great, too! We got the 50/50 split with hidden tilt on all 7 windows. They look and operate beautifully.

The rolling shades look great, but they are more see-through than we had hoped. The swatch held up to a window is a far cry from the whole shade being up. During the night you can see in and during the day you can see out (not so bad, kinda nice actually). We now are discussing cost-effective ways of working with WDG and their factory to get us new rolling shades in our master bedroom. I am hoping that goes well...

Most businesses charge you the remaining amount when the work is completed and not hanging out in a warehouse. < username>
Neil Powell</username>
<time>1435932661074</time><Rating>5</Rating>< text>
It was love at first sight: in 1979, as a young art student, I, like many others of my generation, were captivated by David Hockney‚Äôs supreme draughtsmanship and uncluttered painterly portals onto a cloudless Californian lifestyle.

But a lot has happened since then; Tracey Emin, digital photography, tablet devices, Creative Suite¬©, Instagram¬©, not to mention Barthes‚Äô Camera Lucida - and a whole lot more. To place things into a proper perspective, over the past five decades, Hockney has always been an early adopter of new technologies, bringing both his sensibility and style to acrylic, Polaroid¬© and digital imaging by turns.

The shows at Annely Juda/L.A. Louver are based around what Hockney describes as ‚Äòthe void‚Äô between the convention of perspective, the image surface and the viewer, and though his depiction of this perceptual disjunction may lack the poignancy of Barthes or the incisiveness of Sontag, it also comes with an understanding of the act of seeing along with an understanding of that act embodied in a practice which remains pointedly distinct from any other living artist.

Lest we forget: beyond the words and the technologies, Mr. Hockney still touches paint to canvas with a consummate brilliance that can only be sustained by the combined qualities of determination, practice and talent. This may of course be a statement of the blooming obvious, but even on a bad day, David Hockney remains one of the best painters England ever exported.

But beyond sentiment and back to the present, Hockney‚Äôs latest show is fascinating for a number of reasons; essentially he is attempting to unravel, on our behalf, the conventions of seeing, painting and photography that have become tangled through the convergence of digital and analogue image-making.

The typical portraits that comprise just less than half of the works in the show are apparently a foretaste of some 70 painted portraits that will be shown at major venues next year, and many of these are classic Hockney; stunning lines of brushwork against flattened slabs of intense colour. This juxtapositional use of paint has the effect of rendering the paintings expressive and expressionless at the same time. The portraits offer not only an insight into the artist‚Äôs vision, but also an incidental snapshot of his encounters with individuals in his social and professional orbit. Aesthetically and metaphorically, the deadpan Liquitex¬© flatness of Hockney‚Äôs painting is perfectly suited to the laconic depiction of his models and a sense, not of timelessness, but of subjects slipping into time.

In summary though, there is no implication here that this show is some kind of Curate‚Äôs Egg; it is altogether interesting, with never a dull moment, never a sense that the artist is recumbent on the laurels and always the sense that he is striving for more, for better, and driving hard to understand how human perception sits alongside the sensory extensions offered by technology. After spending an hour here, I just knew it wasn‚Äôt enough.<//text>

A grocery store trapped in the 1980s. I'm not expecting upscale merchandise from a place like this but after looking around and not seeing anything organic, and somewhat barren shelves and little to no options for vegetarians in the way of protein (unless you count beans or the one kind of boca patty they had) I almost walked out.
